  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d7772ca4-340d-412b-84c7-8fadb27ba08e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

  <span id="freeText17306149727983399085" style="display:none">My name is Gwen Frost, and I go to Mythos Academy; a school of myths, magic and warrior whiz kids, where even the lowliest geek knows how to chop off somebody's head with a sword and Logan Quinn, the hottest Spartan guy in school, also happens to be the deadliest. But lately, things have been weird, even for Mythos. First, mean girl Jasmine Ashton was murdered in the Library of Antiquities. Then, someone stole the Bowl of Tears, a magical artifact that can be used to bring about the second Chaos War. You know, death, destruction and lots of other bad, bad things. Freaky stuff like this goes on all the time at Mythos, but I'm determined to find out who killed Jasmine and why; especially since I should have been the one who died...</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_25871069').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_25871069').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_25871069').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {

    Sort of. Jasmine's best friend and boyfriend are hooking up behind her back. Also, Logan and Gwen like each other, but Logan is "dating" (probably sle<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>

So to summarize, a minor love triangle, but not a huge one.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/597115626?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" href="/user/show/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time">Heather K (dentist in my spare time)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11061092-touch-of-frost">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=hated-it">hated-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=ranty-review">ranty-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=price-was-right-2-99-or-less">price-was-right-2-99-or-less</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=group-reading-challenge">group-reading-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=m-f">m-f</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer597115626" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5201302357236035644"><b>I freakin' HATED this book</b><br/><br/>I can summarize why I loathed this book with just a few quotes:<br/><br/><i>"Yucko" (repeated 6 times)<br/><br/>"My Gypsy gift" (repeated 45 times- yes I searched for this on my kindle)<br/><br/>And for the sentiment attached to quotes like this one <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ "I loved Samson; I really did. But he's a guy, after all, and he's always thinking with his dick. I expected this sort of thing from him. But Morgan and I grew up together... That's why she's going to pay for screwing my boyfriend."  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide s</a></span></i></span>
  <span id="freeText5201302357236035644" style="display:none"><b>I freakin' HATED this book</b><br /><br />I can summarize why I loathed this book with just a few quotes:<br /><br /><i>"Yucko" (repeated 6 times)<br /><br />"My Gypsy gift" (repeated 45 times- yes I searched for this on my kindle)<br /><br />And for the sentiment attached to quotes like this one <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ "I loved Samson; I really did. But he's a guy, after all, and he's always thinking with his dick. I expected this sort of thing from him. But Morgan and I grew up together... That's why she's going to pay for screwing my boyfriend."  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></i><br /><br />This book was a HUGE disappointment. I was hoping for another Vampire Academy, something with great sexual tension and a kick-butt plot. Instead I got poorly written crap that is filled with stereotypes. <br /><br />Meet Gwen, a girl who is so nerdy and alternative that she <i>wears hoodies!</i> and <i>reads comic books!</i> Crazy stuff here, folks. Gwen is just a terrible character. She is so judgmental it is sickening. She hates the rich girls and the "sluts" (the ultimate put down in Gwen's book!) and anyone too girly. The worst part is that she doesn't seem to mind male "sluts". Apparently having sex is only a cardinal sin if you have lady parts. <br /><br />She is also incredibly dense. Gwen claims that because of her "Gypsy gift" she can never forget anything. Then why, may I ask, does she seem not to catch on to ANYTHING. I figured out everything from about 60% on and Gwen was still walking around in a befuddled haze. Gwen also seems to have the mental capacity of a 12 year old. She thinks kissing is icky and says things like "yucko" regularly. She is supposed to be <b>17!!!</b>. Honestly, I found that hard to believe. She goes to a magic school with abnormally strong Spartans, Valkyrie girls who shoot colored sparks out of their fingers, and she herself has a "Gypsy gift" of seeing the history of things that she touches yet she still doesn't believe in the Gods and mythology- what more proof do you need girl?!?! And don't get me even started on the "romance". I didn't get it and I wasn't feeling it. <br /><br />The writing too was just not up to par. Aside from the fact that it was incredibly repetitive and cliched, there are tons of grammar mistakes and contradictions. It just irritated me more and more as I read. I tried to keep an open mind but I wanted to put it down at about 70% because I was so frustrated with the whole reading experience. <br /><br />As you can see, this book was a HUGE miss for me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5201302357236035644" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_195536031" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/195536031" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/195536031?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=cute">cute</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=general-fantasy-and-mythology">general-fantasy-and-mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=favorite-book-guys">favorite-book-guys</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer195536031" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5435165908012984398">SKEPTICAL STACIA IS A LITTLE LESS SKEPTICAL TODAY.<br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Bitch," she said. "That was my favorite dagger."<br/>She had a favorite dagger? Seriously? And she thought that I was a freak.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>3.5 stars. Welcome to <b><s>Mythos Academy</s> ... Warrior Academy</b>. Oh sure, there are all kinds of mythical races present, but let's get real here : all I could see was a story about who could kick ass the most. <br/><br/><b>This is like House of Night without the raging diarrhea.</b> Meaning : this book still has the fun adventures, but yo</span>
  <span id="freeText5435165908012984398" style="display:none">SKEPTICAL STACIA IS A LITTLE LESS SKEPTICAL TODAY.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Bitch," she said. "That was my favorite dagger."<br />She had a favorite dagger? Seriously? And she thought that I was a freak.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />3.5 stars. Welcome to <b><s>Mythos Academy</s> ... Warrior Academy</b>. Oh sure, there are all kinds of mythical races present, but let's get real here : all I could see was a story about who could kick ass the most. <br /><br /><b>This is like House of Night without the raging diarrhea.</b> Meaning : this book still has the fun adventures, but you're less likely to want to slap the hell out of each and every character. Honestly, I was sort of expecting something similar to the Covenant series because of the mythology, but this really wasn't the same thing at all. Gwen reminds me a little of Claire from Morganville Vamps (starts off klutzy and unsure of herself, but you can tell she's going to gain her footing as the series proceeds), and the relationship with Gwen and her grandmother reminded me a lot of Zoey and Grandma Redbird from HoN. <br /><br />So okay, we had the insecure lead and the all-too-gorgeous male counterpart, which is pretty stereotypical for the genre, but what can I say? Even I have days when I don't mind the stereotypes. Yes, I can picture your mouths dropping open in shock at that statement coming from me. If a book hooks me, it just does, regardless of how often I've bashed the stereotypes in previous books. Call me a sucker for hot guys who can fight and love to save the damsel in distress, but Logan was pretty swoon-worthy every time he came to Gwen's aid. Cliched, maybe. But it was awfully cute.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"I think so." Logan stared at me, and a smile pulled up his lips. "But maybe you should give me mouth-to-mouth, just to make sure."<br />I rolled my eyes and stood up. "Do you ever think about anything besides sex?"<br />His smile widened. "Not when you're around, Gypsy girl."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Also, I felt like a lot of Gwen's insecurities mirrored real feelings that many of us would have had at that age. Random side note : the signing of the mattresses thing...I KNEW THIS GUY. No joke. I had a friend who did this. Not that you needed to know this info about me, but an ex of mine and I went and hooked up on that guy's bed and signed HIS mattress. Because I'm craaaazy like that.<br /><br />The TENSION (oh-no-he-didn't) issue at the end of the book has me wanting to run out and grab the next book (or just download it because I'm far too lazy to run anywhere). For people who've read the series : <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[am I wrong in guessing that Logan could be Loki's champion, or am I way off? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It's been a while since I've wanted to read book 2 of a series right away. Usually, I don't do this. <br /><br /><b>The few minor issues :</b><br /><br />I didn't mind the cliches this time, but there were a LOT more of them than I'd normally like. Fortunately, the story itself made up for some of this.<br /><br />Friends of mine have mentioned this author's repetitive nature with mundane details. Since this is the first book I've read, I can't confirm that this will keep happening, but I did notice a few details/scenes which were repeated unnecessarily more than once.<br /><br />While the second half of the book was completely awesome, it took me a few chapters to wade past some dull scenes and silly drama. However, given the direction of the second half of the book, I feel like this series has potential to bring it in later books the way that VA did. <br /><br /><b>Overall, I'm excited to have found a new author and series to vibe on!</b> <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5435165908012984398" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4176166-cindy?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy">sci-fi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4176166-cindy?shelf=atlp-review">atlp-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4176166-cindy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4176166-cindy?shelf=arc">arc</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer157792924" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1759622317544685073"><b>This review may also be found on <a><i>A Thousand Little Pages</i></a>.</b><br/><br/>Gwen Frost is being forced to attend Mythos Academy, an elite school set apart to train kids who just so happen to be descendants of various mythical warriors. Of course, Gwen doesn’t believe in any of the supernatural skills her classmates supposedly possess. The only type of magic she actually accepts is her own and that of her own family. When the school’s most popular girl, the icy Valkyrie princess Jasmine, is murdered right in the li</span>
  <span id="freeText1759622317544685073" style="display:none"><b>This review may also be found on <a><i>A Thousand Little Pages</i></a>.</b><br /><br />Gwen Frost is being forced to attend Mythos Academy, an elite school set apart to train kids who just so happen to be descendants of various mythical warriors. Of course, Gwen doesn’t believe in any of the supernatural skills her classmates supposedly possess. The only type of magic she actually accepts is her own and that of her own family. When the school’s most popular girl, the icy Valkyrie princess Jasmine, is murdered right in the library next to a stolen mythical artifact called the Bowl of Tears, Gwen is determined to get to the bottom of the entire situation. It’s never a good idea to poke your head into other people’s business, though. So the results? Who else is to blame but yourself?<br /><br /><i>Touch of Frost</i> belongs to the new batch of paranormal stories that all seem exactly the same, only with different character names and fantastical elements. This novel’s back story is a mishmash of tons of various warriors -- from Norse gods to ninjas. While that is certainly a nice idea, it’s never really delved into. Except for a few key warrior gods, all the others felt extraneous and were barely mentioned at all.<br /><br />The characters aren’t especially mind-blowing, either. You have the blonde mean girl clique, the quirky and unpopular heroine, and the hot bad boy who falls in love with the heroine anyways; just the same formula used over and over and over again. The character with an actual personality was Vic, the ancient magical sword, who has a grand total of about five lines in the entire novel. That is just sad. A sword beats out all those other full-fledged human characters? Sad, sad, sad.<br /><br /><i>Touch of Frost</i> is quite a cliché, but lovers of stereotypical teen paranormal stories (I know there are a lot of you out there) will devour it with glee.<br /><br />Book Source: ARC via Flamingnet</span>
  <a data-text-id="1759622317544685073" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_193266367" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/193266367" />
    <a title="Sabrina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5771244-sabrina"><img alt="Sabrina" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/193266367?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sabrina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sabrina" href="/user/show/5771244-sabrina">Sabrina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780758272607" href="/book/show/10928051-touch-of-frost">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5771244-sabrina?shelf=blacklist-of-bad-books">blacklist-of-bad-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer193266367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11729811698149973359">Everything that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/193791375' rel='nofollow noopener'>I've already said</a> for the prequel still stands.<br/>And in this one we get a shitload of pumpkins, too.<br/>Seriously, I don't understand the pumpkins.<br/>I don't understand the fixation with the designer clothes, either. In every paragraph we are reminded that everyone in that school wears designer clothes. And that there are pumpkins.<br/>From now on, I'm going to cram pumpkins everywhere just to prove how annoying they are. <br/><br/>Well, I suppose now it's time to say something review-like.<br/>Our heroine (</span>
  <span id="freeText11729811698149973359" style="display:none">Everything that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/193791375" rel="nofollow noopener">I've already said</a> for the prequel still stands.<br>And in this one we get a shitload of pumpkins, too.<br>Seriously, I don't understand the pumpkins.<br>I don't understand the fixation with the designer clothes, either. In every paragraph we are reminded that everyone in that school wears designer clothes. And that there are pumpkins.<br>From now on, I'm going to cram pumpkins everywhere just to prove how annoying they are. <br><br>Well, I suppose now it's time to say something review-like.<br>Our heroine (pumpkin! <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380355503i/707669.png" width="12" height="12" class="gr-hostedUserImg">) has the gift of being able to tell the history of every object by touching it (that works even for pumpkins!).<br>So this could have been a story telling how this girl became a stellar detective, who solved every case just by touching some odd scrap of evidence. It could even have been the story of this girl becoming a famous historian, who unveiled weird events about weirder artifacts by simply touching them. Or a Doctor House with a skirt, diagnosing unknown exotic diseases (or healing sick pumpkins).<br>I could go on for hours, but the sad truth is that this novel is none of the above.<br>The girl uses her gift to retrieve stuff for her schoolmates, in exchange of petty cash.<br>Just sad, isn't it?<br>Even the pumpkins are sad for that:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488184832i/22087370.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So, this girl has this fantabulous gift. The author reminds us of it every single page, but sometimes the protagonist herself forgets (how could she! Call the avenging pumpkins!)<br><blockquote>My dad, Tyr, had died from cancer when I was two, and the only memories I had of him were the faded photos my mom had shown me.</blockquote><br>See? She FORGETS. She could just touch something and have full knowledge of everything concerning her father.<br>This happens a lot, throughout the entire book.<br>Bad editor, no cookie!<br>But you can have a pumpkin, here it is: <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488184832i/22087371.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Our girl then goes to a special school for magical kids. Think of Hogwarts, but without the medieval stuff and full of mythological nonsense.<br>There she finds a lot of other magical kids who all have some special superpower and wear designer clothes. It’s important to highlight that second aspect again, you know.<br>And there are pumpkin fudges, pumpkin rolls and other pumpkins.<br>All very interesting.<br><br>Do I have to go on?<br>I think you can get the gist of it.<br>There's some abs-staring and some oh-no-I-didnt-think-you-liked-me-even-though-you-tried-to-kiss-me. Quite uneventful. And boring. And don't forget the pumpkins.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11729811698149973359" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_158966555" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/158966555" />
    <a title="oliviasbooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks"><img alt="oliviasbooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1257619306p2/2843533.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/158966555?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="oliviasbooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="oliviasbooks" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks">oliviasbooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780758272607" href="/book/show/10928051-touch-of-frost">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those addicted to parormal boarding-schools</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=urban-fantasy-paranormal">urban-fantasy-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=e-version">e-version</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=boarding-school-plot">boarding-school-plot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=other-creatures">other-creatures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=high-expectations">high-expectations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=read-2012">read-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=mystery-crime-sleuthing">mystery-crime-sleuthing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=wring-her-neck">wring-her-neck</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=paranormal-humans">paranormal-humans</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer158966555" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17228421864290750604">"Yucko"". That is the heroine's favorite word. And it fits, a bit. However, if I were to blurb the paranormal sleutheress boarding-school romance ""Touch of Frost"" I would say ""Likable, but in the direct vicinity of 'meh'"".<br/><br/>I feel a little bit like venting, but I am in bed with a cold. So, please excuse me for amassing random thoughts here instead of a structured review: <br/><br/>- English is not my mother tongue. Therefore I am always happy to pick up additional tidbits that help me to understand and </span>
  <span id="freeText17228421864290750604" style="display:none">"Yucko"". That is the heroine's favorite word. And it fits, a bit. However, if I were to blurb the paranormal sleutheress boarding-school romance ""Touch of Frost"" I would say ""Likable, but in the direct vicinity of 'meh'"".<br /><br />I feel a little bit like venting, but I am in bed with a cold. So, please excuse me for amassing random thoughts here instead of a structured review: <br /><br />- English is not my mother tongue. Therefore I am always happy to pick up additional tidbits that help me to understand and use it better. While reading ""Touch of Frost"", I learned that ""purple hoodie"" is actually a composite word. The same might be true for ""violet eyes"", a narrower term being ""my violet eyes"". The broader term can be found sixteen times within this series' starter volume. Both can be used in sentences of remarkable literary value, i.e.: <i>""So I just stared at him, my feelings for him so obvious in my violet eyes.""</i> The only way Gwenny could be so unwaveringly sure of the expressability of her Frost-Familiy-Brand-Eyes in PANTONE 261C is extensive self-study via mirror... or it might be that the author still has no idea how a first-person-narration is successfully implemented. That might also explain the long, long and kind of repetitive analytical monologues the heroine has in her mind - preferably in the face of imminent danger.<br /><br />- Connected to the point-of-view is a lot of meta-information that gets dumped on the reader, which is either the result of judging the readers as being too dense to spot the author's applaudable ability to stick to certain paranomal romance or sleuthing-story formula on the dot on his or her own or it is a tell-tale-sign of parodistic writing. I tend to go with the first possibility. <br />Gwendolyn actually tells us <i>""Everything about Logan screamed <u>bad boy</u>, from the thick, silky, ink-black hair to his intense ice blue eyes to the black leather jacket that highlighted his broad shoulders.""</i> A thousand things just feel ""off"" to the heroine, which certainly makes her investigate. But then she misses some important clues. And in case the reader has not just noticed that things are a tad too obvious here and the heroine has a plot-lengthening moment, she emphasises her own being behind: <i>""I felt a memory stirring in my subconscious. Something to do with illusions. Something that I'd seen or heard or read or thought about in the last few days. Something that was important.""</i> Well, duh.<br /><br />- In addition there is the ""let's-have-a-paranormal-heroine-but-how-on-earth-can-we-make-use-of-her-powers"" dilemma. In ""Touch of Frost"" it is not as bad as in, for example, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6963749.Clarity__Clarity___1_" title="Clarity (Clarity, #1) by Kim Harrington" rel="nofollow noopener">Clarity</a>. But if the heroine would play her cards, or rather abilities, right, there would be no need for her to admit repeatedly that she is no Veronica Mars. Gwen, whose gift is ""touch magic"" - having visions when touching people or people's objects -, breaks into a room to find clues about a murder, but actually tries to avoid touching most things in there. She takes out a book with a sticky note tacked to a rather relevant looking paragraph, but a day later she has still not tried her power on it. Gwen's reluctance is feebly explained away by her fear of reliving horrible moments or learning secrets without the consent of people she respects, but in the light of solving the case - and the fact, that Gwen earns money by locating lost and sometimes embarrassing stuff - that sounds far-fetched.<br /><br />- The heroine's ""I-avoid-touching-people"" strategy certainly works beautifully with the ""Save-the-heroine's-virginity-for-the-last-installment-or-forever"" rule most paranormal young adult romance sticks to. Gwenny is even of the unkissed sort and ohhh does she want to make out with the bad, but life-saving boy, but then she would compromise him by learning all his and his family's dirty secrets and probably his hot and dirty thoughts on top. Therefore she takes down her open arms in time, makes a double morron out of herself verbally, has the love interest's half-melted ice-eyes turn to popsicles and does not get a third chance in the end, because by then we have - just in time - switched to the moody-broody ""I-cannot-have-you-know-my-dark-secret-and-my-utterly-ugly-side-yet-although-I-crave-you"" part of the required plot development. Who would have guessed, huh?<br /><br />That would be all for now. Before you say it, I have to bring it on the table myself: I cannot successfully explain what made me read a paranormal boarding school romance <i>again</i> after so many disappointments. Must have been the high average rating plus the enthusiasm of several of my friends - <i>or</i> my indestructable hope that Enid Blython and J. K. Rowlings <i>cannot</i> be the only ones who were able to pull off addictive stories set in boarding school environments.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17228421864290750604" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5312128098248353437"><br/><b>DNF at 41%</b><br/><br/>This just isn't doing it for me. Maybe it's because I'm fighting off the sickness and have no time for nonsense, or maybe I just need to stop making excuses for this.<br/><br/>I've never been a fan of slut shaming. I'm especially not a fan of slut shaming when it's sexist and one-sided. To Gwen, chicks who sleep around are sluts and whores. Logan, however, who has been in every girl in school's bed, is <i>sexy, mysterious, and dark</i> when he does it. She even goes so far as to say she understands why</span>
  <span id="freeText5312128098248353437" style="display:none"><br><b>DNF at 41%</b><br><br>This just isn't doing it for me. Maybe it's because I'm fighting off the sickness and have no time for nonsense, or maybe I just need to stop making excuses for this.<br><br>I've never been a fan of slut shaming. I'm especially not a fan of slut shaming when it's sexist and one-sided. To Gwen, chicks who sleep around are sluts and whores. Logan, however, who has been in every girl in school's bed, is <i>sexy, mysterious, and dark</i> when he does it. She even goes so far as to say she understands why he sleeps around, because his body is just so perfect. Wait, what? Yeah... but don't you dare be a chick with big boobs, or it's straight to hell for you!<br><br>I also couldn't find any spare fucks to give over who murdered Jasmine. Seems I'm all out of fucks. I should make a note to stop and get more from the store on the way home from work...<br><br>Finally, if I have to hear one more god-damned-blasted-time how Gwen is <i>different</i> and just <i>doesn't fit in</i> at Mythos, my next step will be to start sawing off the end of a shotgun. Seriously. WE GET IT GWEN, YOU ARE A SPECIAL FUCKING SNOWFLAKE who happens to be poor and a geek in the midst of the preppy and rich. Go feel guilty about your dead mother some more. I don't see how that could possibly be unhealthy. You'll turn out fine.<br><br>And because this review would be incomplete with out a zero fucks gif (how could I deprive you like that?), I give you one of my favorites:<br><br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.com/i/npypyg" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_569403096" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/569403096" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/569403096?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=boarding-school">boarding-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer569403096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8674795980213560369">Ugh, what's with the slut shaming? So one girl at her school is beautiful, popular, and sleeps around. That's not exactly admirable behavior, but to bring it to the front and judge her and secretly slut shame her and have other characters talk about it behind her back is not cool. Jasmine's not the only character that Gwen names as a slut either, Logan Quinn supposedly sleeps around. Again, typical teenager behavior, and bringing it up constantly doesn't make for an entirely likable character wh</span>
  <span id="freeText8674795980213560369" style="display:none">Ugh, what's with the slut shaming? So one girl at her school is beautiful, popular, and sleeps around. That's not exactly admirable behavior, but to bring it to the front and judge her and secretly slut shame her and have other characters talk about it behind her back is not cool. Jasmine's not the only character that Gwen names as a slut either, Logan Quinn supposedly sleeps around. Again, typical teenager behavior, and bringing it up constantly doesn't make for an entirely likable character when it says something that said character is judgmental like that.<br /><br />The book is just all right, the idea of an academy full of descendants of legendary warriors and servants of the gods is nice, but oh god, Gwen does not fit in. And it's not only that, she is such a little whiner about it; I'm reminded of the goth and emo kids at my school who whines about everything and goes against the establishment just for the sake of being contrary. Gwen is like that, and she's not a very sympathetic character in my eyes. She's also hypocritical, since she breaks the rules herself by sneaking out of school to visit her grandmother every few days.<br /><br />New premise, but not an entirely promising nor attractive one. Whiny, annoying lead character. Will continue the series, but only because I'm bored and lacking reading materials.</span>

<div id="review_636941971" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/636941971" />
    <a title="Mizuki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki"><img alt="Mizuki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368277474p2/16842102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/636941971?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2013</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer636941971" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6127117123704248269">1.5 stars. This book is one of those <i>"Oh I'm the poor, humble girl who has to go to a school filled with spoiled rich kids"</i> books. We're all supposed to be guilt trapped into feeling bad for the poor heroine, but sadly I found myself being annoyed by both the main character and the story.<br/><br/>The author, Jennifer Estep tried very hard to make her heroine and her story humorous, but both come off very forced and awkward. Not to mention the 'heroine' also loves to label people with stereotypes such as </span>
  <span id="freeText6127117123704248269" style="display:none">1.5 stars. This book is one of those <i>"Oh I'm the poor, humble girl who has to go to a school filled with spoiled rich kids"</i> books. We're all supposed to be guilt trapped into feeling bad for the poor heroine, but sadly I found myself being annoyed by both the main character and the story.<br /><br />The author, Jennifer Estep tried very hard to make her heroine and her story humorous, but both come off very forced and awkward. Not to mention the 'heroine' also loves to label people with stereotypes such as 'the band geek', 'the slut' and 'the spoiled brat' and so on, such attitude makes her rather unlikable. <br /><br />Yes, we're treated with tons and tons of slut shaming. And according to the heroine, a girl sleeping around with boys is a slut and a bitch, but a bad boy who sneaked out from girl's dorm and asked another girl whom he had barely spoken to before to "get back to his dorm" makes the boy a sexy dangerous bad boy? Oh....this is double standards.<br /><br />There's also no sense of reality in Estep's mythology and the magical school for mythical warriors. Supposedly all students and professors were trained and prepared to battle the evil villains but their actions and how they handle the incident of a girl student being murdered on campus shows me none of them---even the professors who are adults, can handle serious issues logically and maturely. I mean, no one ever thinks about searching the murdered girl's dorm for evident or questioning her friends in order to find the murderer? Are you kidding me!? So the whole thing looks just damn fake and make-believe. Ms. Estep, why don't you take a writing lesson before you start writing anything else in the future?<br /><br />Last but not least, how the murder mystery is revealed at the very end is so cliched and forced---so the bad guy wastes time to inform-dumps the entire evil plan to the heroine, instead of finishing her off then and there!? It's so cliched that it reads like some badly written detective novels. It also reminds me of how J K. Rowling reveals the 'mysteries' of each of her Harry Potter book (I'm referring on the ones I did bother to read, you know).</span>
  <a data-text-id="6127117123704248269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText12778389849349984635" style="display:none"> <b> "Come inside and all will be revealed" </b><br /><br /><br />Originally what caught my interest was that this book reminded me of Vampire Academy except mythical creatures instead of vampires. I was <i>not </i> disappointed. From the first page this author caught my attention and I was eager to learn more about Gwen, Mythos Academy, Daphne, and <i>Spartan-Licious</i> <b> "Logan freaking Quinn" </b> <br /><br />Meet Gwen Frost, she's a gypsy, an outcast, a nerd and a comic book fanatic. She's one of my new favorite protagonist! She's also witty, charming, fun loving, empatic and smart. <br /><br /><b> "So," the Valkyrie said, cracking open the lid of her Perrier. "This is where you eat lunch. All the way in the back here. What are you? A vampire who's afraid of sunlight or something?"<br /><br /> Vampires? Were vampires real too? I wondered but I didn't want to look stupid and ask, especially since I didn't know what Daphne was doing here in the first place.<br /><br /> "Yeah," I said in a guarded voice. "You caught me. I've got this whole superhero thing going on, so I sit way back here to keep the paparazzi and rabid fans at bay." </b> <br /><br />Since tragedy struck at home six months ago she's been uprooted to Mythos Academy where Gwen finds herself surrounded by mythical warriors of all types. <b> Spartans, Romans, Valkyrie, Amazons </b> and she's the lonely new <b> Gypsy </b> on the block. As you learn these whiz kids ferociously powerful warrior gifts are compatible with the mythical creatures in <i> Clash Of The Titans </i> whereas Gwen's gift of Psychometry appears to be no match for their talent and skills, or so it may seem.<br /><br /> <b> Psychometry </b> is the ability to touch someone and read their emotions, thoughts, interests and deepest dark secrets. she's quickly labelled as a "freak", "a nobody", but she easily proves to herself that she's "not a nobody." <br /> <br />Gwen's new unlikely friend a rich, popular Valkyrie Daphne was an excitingly charismatic supporting character. <br /><br /><b> "Let me walk you to your room,"Logan offered in a helpful voice. "You, me and the Gypsy girl could have our own <br />bonfire tonight." <br /><br />Daphne and I stared at eachother. I rolled my eyes while Daphne sniffed. <br /><br />"Oh please,"she scoffed. "Like I need a guy to protect me. I'm a Valkyrie, remember? I could pick you up and break your back over my knee, Spartan. Like you were a piñata."<br /><br />"Kinky," Logan said, smiling at her. "I like it." <br /></b><br /><br />Overall this book is an easy 5 stars because I <b> LOVED</b> it! The next book <u> Kiss Of Frost </u> comes out late this year as well. I'm eagerly looking forward to catching up with Gwen's life at Mythos Academy now that she's discovered her true Gypsy heritage while shes learning her inherited magical powers, as well as Daphne, and of course <b> <s> The Spartan-Licious</s> "Logan freaking Quinn" ;)<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Like what you see here, check out more of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://missvainsparanormalfantasy.com/">http://missvainsparanormalfantasy.com/</a><br /></b></span>

<div id="review_238323336" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/238323336" />
    <a title="Rayne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5374178-rayne"><img alt="Rayne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440598663p2/5374178.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/238323336?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rayne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rayne" href="/user/show/5374178-rayne">Rayne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=characters-flat-as-a-board">characters-flat-as-a-board</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=totally-saw-that-coming">totally-saw-that-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=slut-shaming">slut-shaming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=your-sexism-is-not-welcome-here">your-sexism-is-not-welcome-here</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=school-life">school-life</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=can-i-get-my-hours-back">can-i-get-my-hours-back</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer238323336" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3292216365414510901">The book had an interesting premise, even if somewhat sketchy. I liked some of its concepts, but the protagonist completely ruined any chance this book had with me. <br/><br/><br/>------Edit 6/02/2012<br/><br/>I hated this book. In case the 1 star rating wasn't clear enough, I absolutely despised it. I gave it 2 stars at first, because I really hate giving books a 1 star rating. I do give out 1 star ratings when a book deserves it, but I like thinking that (almost) every book has something to offer. But, after sleeping </span>
  <span id="freeText3292216365414510901" style="display:none">The book had an interesting premise, even if somewhat sketchy. I liked some of its concepts, but the protagonist completely ruined any chance this book had with me. <br /><br /><br />------Edit 6/02/2012<br /><br />I hated this book. In case the 1 star rating wasn't clear enough, I absolutely despised it. I gave it 2 stars at first, because I really hate giving books a 1 star rating. I do give out 1 star ratings when a book deserves it, but I like thinking that (almost) every book has something to offer. But, after sleeping on it, I came back the next day and got a great amount of pleasure out of giving this one the single, lonely star I feel it deserves. I know I'm in the minority here, seeing as how this book has an overall rating of over 4 stars, but I really fail to see the appeal of this one, and it is not because of a lack of trying. While reading it, I gave up on this book three times. Three freaking times I put it aside, completely decided to never bother with it again, but I came back again and again. I just want to make it clear that I did not come back because I was intrigued or because I wanted to know the big "mystery": Everything about this book is ridiculously predictable right from the start. The reason I came back was because I kept hoping I could see what everyone was raving about. I think the 1 star rating makes it pretty clear that I never stumbled upon what makes this book deserve the praise.<br /><br />Gwen is one of the most detestable characters I've ever had the misfortune of reading about. She's right up there with Luce, Nora and Zoey in the list of characters I wish I could erase from literary existence by flushing them down a toilet. She's whiny, judgmental, self-absorbed, self-righteous, oh, and she wants me to remind you that she has no friends. God, I swear she said that last thing about 50 times per chapter. Please, remind me how much of a loner and a rebel you are about five freaking times per page, I don't get tired of it at all. Oh, and you wear hoodies and read comic books? Wow, that is so interesting and original and totally explains why absolutely no one gets you. (Yeah, right. Guess what? That was me in high school and that never had as a result a shortage of friends or cruel rejection from everyone.) And, of course, Gwen is a loner because she's not as rich or as "pretty" or as "special" as the rest of the mean girls in class, when the truth is she actually is, but, of course, she just doesn't know it. But that's okay. Gwen comforts herself by declaring all the other girls "raging sluts" and knowing that no matter what she does, says, wears or who she likes, she will never be like those "raging sluts". The whole characterization of one of the pseudo-antagonists in the story is that she is gorgeous and is only popular because she's been with every boy in school and likes labels and brands and is mean to poor little Gwen. Sounds familiar? Yes, like every other generic YA mean girl out there. And the plot is not that different, either.<br /><br />There's really nothing original about this book. I considered giving this one extra points for bringing different types of warriors and mythical creatures into one school until I realized that, not only is the whole concept far-fetched in itself, the book never offers a real explanation for it. Oh well, I suppose it does. The school is supposed to train all these warriors for a war that even the protagonists is convinced is just a whole lot of superstitious bogus. Which if you think about it, for a girl that has powers and lives constantly surrounded by mythical warriors like the Valkyries to not believe that there could be a war with other mythical beings, well, it's pretty stupid all-around. <br /><br />This book was really infuriating and frustrating. There's barely a plot in there, but I couldn't be bothered to follow it anyway when I had to see it flow through a character like Gwen, who is ready to judge and insult and scorn everyone around her but falls for a guy that's popular because he hurts people and signs the mattresses of all the girls he sleeps with on campus, because, of course, that makes him so hot. There's no character development in this book, no real mystery driving the plot, a ridiculous resolution that continues to belittle girls and furthers the stereotype about the mean girls and condemns woman sexuality, an interesting, but ultimately unsatisfying concept and a terrible lead I wish I could bleach out of my mind. It's been, what?, 3 or 4 months since I read this one and I still can't get over how much it disappointed and angered me. The thing is that I was actually expecting a lot out of this one, but a book like this one is nothing but a slap in the face to YA readers out there. It's nothing but a generic, formulaic story that has been done many times because someone out there believes we are not smart enough to recognize it for what it is, throw in there a bunch of high school stereotypes and some half-assed mythology to make it paranormal, and there you go. To conclude this rant, I vow to never read any more books in this series and to try my very best to even forget I wasted my time reading this. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3292216365414510901" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2292296429" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2292296429" />
    <a title="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog"><img alt="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352609417p2/2489554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2292296429?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)" href="/user/show/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog">Annie (Under the Covers Book Blog)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=author-jennifer-estep">author-jennifer-estep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=genre-young-adult">genre-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489554-annie-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=series-mythos-academy">series-mythos-academy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2292296429" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16809882596476070426"><a href='http://www.underthecoversbookblog.com/2018/02/review-touch-of-frost-by-jennifer-estep.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430489640i/14717740.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a> <br/><br/>After reading the first book of the spin-off series, I was curious enough to know where the story started so I decided to go back and read this series. I’ve been a fan of Jennifer Estep’s writing for a long time now and I have to say that this series definitely falls in line with the rest of her excellent quality.<br/><br/>Firstly, I was most intrigued about the heroine, Gwen in this series. She’s a whole lot different than Rory and I think that’s a good thing. My favorite thing about Gwen’s characte</span>
  <span id="freeText16809882596476070426" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.underthecoversbookblog.com/2018/02/review-touch-of-frost-by-jennifer-estep.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430489640i/14717740.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><br>After reading the first book of the spin-off series, I was curious enough to know where the story started so I decided to go back and read this series. I’ve been a fan of Jennifer Estep’s writing for a long time now and I have to say that this series definitely falls in line with the rest of her excellent quality.<br><br>Firstly, I was most intrigued about the heroine, Gwen in this series. She’s a whole lot different than Rory and I think that’s a good thing. My favorite thing about Gwen’s character is the fact that she thinks a lot like a normal teenager. These days, I feel like Young Adult books are becoming more Adult in nature. The themes tend to be more complex and are all about great responsibility that you can easily lose sight of the true essence of a Young Adult novel. Gwen’s narration and the trials and tribulations that she goes through in this novel are something a normal teenager can relate to and for me, that’s what makes me love this series so much. It captures the Young Adult essence, but still has the quality of a excellently written novel.<br><br>The other thing that I think sets this series apart from others is the variety of paranormal species that are present here. Gwen is a Gypsy, but there are so many other species here that it will cater to everyone. It also gives the author so much room to play. It kind of reminds me of Kresley Cole’s Immortals After Dark but the Young Adult version whereas the writing and school setting reminds me of Richelle Mead’s Vampire Academy. If you’re a fan of both authors, then you’re going to enjoy this one.<br><br>TOUCH OF FROST definitely has me intrigued and I will definitely be looking to read more of the books in this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16809882596476070426" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_184300979" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/184300979" />
    <a title="Jen Davis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis"><img alt="Jen Davis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548427639p2/4669344.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/184300979?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen Davis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen Davis" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis">Jen Davis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4669344-jen-davis?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4669344-jen-davis?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4669344-jen-davis?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer184300979" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12617910030329963606">I don't usually read YA fiction, but I am a big fan of Jennifer Estep's Elemental Assassin books... and that is what led me to this first installment of her new Mythos Academy series.<br/><br/><br/>The story centers on a teenage Gypsy named Gwen. She has the give of psychometry, which means she gets psychic impressions from the things she touches. Shortly after the death of her mom, Gwen's grandmother enrolled her in the Mythos Academy, a school for teenagers with special gifts. The halls are filled with Valky</span>
  <span id="freeText12617910030329963606" style="display:none">I don't usually read YA fiction, but I am a big fan of Jennifer Estep's Elemental Assassin books... and that is what led me to this first installment of her new Mythos Academy series.<br /><br /><br />The story centers on a teenage Gypsy named Gwen. She has the give of psychometry, which means she gets psychic impressions from the things she touches. Shortly after the death of her mom, Gwen's grandmother enrolled her in the Mythos Academy, a school for teenagers with special gifts. The halls are filled with Valkyrie, Amazons, Spartans, and other skilled warriors. But Gwen feels out-of-place. She's no warrior and she certainly doesn't come from the privileged background of her peers.<br /><br />Things go from bad to worse for Gwen when she discovers the bloody body of the most popular girl in school in the library. In the aftermath, she is shocked to see that no one is mourning for the dead girl and no one wants to dig beneath the surface to solve her murder. So Gwen decides she will use her powers to figure out what really happened to Jasmine. The story follows her investigation and people who enter her life as a result.<br /><br />This book has the same easy and relaxed writing style I've grown to love from Estep. Her books use simple and clear language which allows you to forget about the words and focus on the story. The concept of the series is pretty good, though not entirely groundbreaking. Gwen is a likeable heroine. And Estep does well to advance her story while still leaving the door open for much more in future books.<br /><br />I liked the book, but I didn't love it. My biggest problem was in the repetition of thoughts we got from Gwen, especially in the first half of the book... her what-if's about her mom, her guilt, her angst, her same questions and reflections over and over. It did peter out before it drove me crazy, but I couldn't quite ignore it. Also, I didn't like how things played out with Logan, the love interest. I know Gwen was supposed to feel jerked around, but dammit, <i>I</i> felt jerked around by his hot-and-cold behavior. And while I know this is an ongoing story, I'm a stickler for an HEA, and I was annoyed by the resolution of this part of the storyline... or lack thereof.<br /><br />I did enjoy watching Gwen begin her transition into something more than she was at the beginning of the story. I think over the course of the series, she is really going to blossom and that will be what makes the books shine. 4 stars.<br /><br /><i>*ARC Provided by author for review</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12617910030329963606" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_600926680" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/600926680" />
    <a title="Natalia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4559407-natalia"><img alt="Natalia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1376311442p2/4559407.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/600926680?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalia" href="/user/show/4559407-natalia">Natalia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4559407-natalia?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4559407-natalia?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4559407-natalia?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4559407-natalia?shelf=1st-person-pov">1st-person-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4559407-natalia?shelf=made-me-laugh">made-me-laugh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4559407-natalia?shelf=boarding-school">boarding-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4559407-natalia?shelf=slut-shaming">slut-shaming</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer600926680" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9007312812706132622">2.5 stars<br/>This is yet another book that I was very enthusiastic about in the beginning, but then my critical thinking kicked in and ruined all the fun. Again. Sometimes I wish I could turn it off, but the more books I read, the more impossible it gets. <br/><br/>I liked the boarding school setting and the mythological aspect of the story, and I really, <i>really</i> tried not to judge our female lead Gwen too harshly, but she made it nearly impossible. Probably because Gwen herself was way too judgmental for my t</span>
  <span id="freeText9007312812706132622" style="display:none">2.5 stars<br />This is yet another book that I was very enthusiastic about in the beginning, but then my critical thinking kicked in and ruined all the fun. Again. Sometimes I wish I could turn it off, but the more books I read, the more impossible it gets. <br /><br />I liked the boarding school setting and the mythological aspect of the story, and I really, <i>really</i> tried not to judge our female lead Gwen too harshly, but she made it nearly impossible. Probably because Gwen herself was way too judgmental for my taste, labeling people right and left. Seriously, it looked like there were no normal nice kids in the academy, and every girl was a bitch or a slut, or some combination of both. Well, except for Daphne, who stopped being a bitch only after she became friends with Gwen. Figures. Obviously, that’s not a way to view other people if you want to make friends with them. <br />Also, I found it hardly believable for a supposedly smart person who was practically surrounded by magic to live in such denial of all things supernatural and mythological, and to have such a condescending approach in regards to every mythology related subject at her school. Seriously, Gwen? Magic mumbo-jumbo?<br />And I felt like the definition between good and evil was too simplistic. Us versus them. Good gods against a bad god Loki. One evil guy among the saintly Pantheon. Now, mythology is not a subject I’m good at, but can we really classify all other deities as do-gooders? Can we? I don’t think so.<br />Of course, there were also things I enjoyed. This book was entertaining and written with humor, with just the right amount of sassiness. Gwen wasn’t overly snarky and her POV made me laugh sometimes. (I can’t help but compare her to Jessie from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17370021.Darker_Days__The_Darker_Agency___1_" title="Darker Days (The Darker Agency, #1) by Jus Accardo" rel="nofollow noopener">Darker Days</a>, who was so excessively snarky it was irritating).<br />Vic the sword was a fun character, grumpy and brutally honest. I wish we had a little more from his POV. <br />And I liked the idea of illusions and how it was realized in the story. <br /><i>“…Once a person believes in an illusion, it’s real to them. Once you believe in something, you give it life and form and substance.”</i><br /><br />I’m not going to comment a lot on the love interest Logan Quinn yet. What do we learn about him? He’s a man-whore. (Is there really anyone who is not a whore in this freaking academy!?? LOL.) He has a knack for killing anything with any weapon. He is strong and scary, sexy and beautiful (according to Gwen). And he obviously has some BIG secret. I think I know who/what he really might be. But maybe I’m wrong. We’ll see.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9007312812706132622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16307977599763501650">I've read this ages ago. I never really processed the book, and the only reason I remembered it is because I've donated my old paperbacks to charity recently. <br/><br/>This type of books were a dime a dozen riding into popularity on a trail of stars like Vampire Academy and the like. Touch of Frost was uninspired, filled with cliche's and tropes. It based it's school for superfreaks on Greek Mythology.<br/><br/>The romance was your classic bad boy meets the unpopular girl, while the mean cheerleader and her cronie</span>
  <span id="freeText16307977599763501650" style="display:none">I've read this ages ago. I never really processed the book, and the only reason I remembered it is because I've donated my old paperbacks to charity recently. <br /><br />This type of books were a dime a dozen riding into popularity on a trail of stars like Vampire Academy and the like. Touch of Frost was uninspired, filled with cliche's and tropes. It based it's school for superfreaks on Greek Mythology.<br /><br />The romance was your classic bad boy meets the unpopular girl, while the mean cheerleader and her cronies conspire against her.<br /><br />The rest of the plot was so random and unconnected, truth be told – I found the story not worth the paper it was printed on. But hey ho, the kiddies loved it.</span>
